  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d5d2da27-706d-42b0-aa59-49d6571bce6f'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<div id="review_119785233" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119785233" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119785233?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=alternating-pov">alternating-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=laugh-aloud">laugh-aloud</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119785233" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8800022420665749545">Sweet, fun, entertaining.. I'm glad I read it!<br/>After reading "Leaving paradise" I was so disappointed that I didn't really want to read the sequel. The first book started so damn good but it was just ok by the middle (except some good parts), and then it ended in such a hurry - I understand why, but i still don't like it. I just couldn't relate to the story at all (I know a lot of people loved it, I just wasn't one of them). <br/><br/>But today I read (and finished) "Return to paradise" and it was really g</span>
  <span id="freeText8800022420665749545" style="display:none">Sweet, fun, entertaining.. I'm glad I read it!<br>After reading "Leaving paradise" I was so disappointed that I didn't really want to read the sequel. The first book started so damn good but it was just ok by the middle (except some good parts), and then it ended in such a hurry - I understand why, but i still don't like it. I just couldn't relate to the story at all (I know a lot of people loved it, I just wasn't one of them). <br><br>But today I read (and finished) "Return to paradise" and it was really good. I can't think of a single thing I didn't like about this book. Short review: nice story line, better characters and lots of funny moments.<br><br>The story is really sweet after all the drama they had in the first volume and (as an improvement) the characters are stronger, making the sequel better. I like the new confident Maggie, I like the dialog between Maggie and Caleb, I like the hot-and-cold game they play and there are so many funny moments that my face hurts for so much laughing.. it's HILARIOUS! I love funny books and I love Lenny and Trish and the teasing between them (also between the main characters).. there was such a great chemistry in this book, and all the characters were so full of life! The action felt so natural page after page, I just felt I was part of the story, never getting bored, always wanting more. <br>It's a great book. If you like sweet-funny romances then you will love it too. I know I do :)<br><br>PS: This is my favorite book from Simone E. (after "perfect chemistry")<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380313075i/688704.jpg" alt="" width="361" height="116" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_270384958" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/270384958" />
    <a title="Annie Brewer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5315988-annie-brewer"><img alt="Annie Brewer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442496062p2/5315988.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/270384958?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie Brewer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie Brewer" href="/user/show/5315988-annie-brewer">Annie Brewer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone who has ever wanted to give up in life</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Annie by: </span>
      Maida 
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=absolutely-amazingly-awesome">absolutely-amazingly-awesome</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=nook-books">nook-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=irresistable-hot-guys">irresistable-hot-guys</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer270384958" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15027354163472064786">OMG! That was the most beautifully poignant book ever!!!! God, I'm such a cry baby!!! It ended perfectly! It had such a beautiful message and left you feeling so good. I am so happy for Caleb and Maggie!! Leah stepped up her game in this one and really surprised me! I loved her! I loved Lenny and Julio and Trish and Damon once again impressed me and Lou was awesome!! I loved everything about this book. I've been on such a Contemp kick that these stories move me beyond words. I am crying from hap</span>
  <span id="freeText15027354163472064786" style="display:none">OMG! That was the most beautifully poignant book ever!!!! God, I'm such a cry baby!!! It ended perfectly! It had such a beautiful message and left you feeling so good. I am so happy for Caleb and Maggie!! Leah stepped up her game in this one and really surprised me! I loved her! I loved Lenny and Julio and Trish and Damon once again impressed me and Lou was awesome!! I loved everything about this book. I've been on such a Contemp kick that these stories move me beyond words. I am crying from happiness to such an aweful circumstance but I'm also crying because Maggie and Caleb's story has come to an end. They will remain in my heart forever! Caleb has become a top fictional boyfriend! He's perfect in everyway!!! This isn't my actual review. I just can't stop tearing up. So I shall return with a full review soon!<br /><br />***********************************************************************<br /><br />Okay, now that I am not such an emotional baby, I can continue with this review. First of all, I love this cover. It really fits this book kinda perfectly. I don't really like the girl that much but the guy is not too bad as my beloved Caleb. <br /><br /><br />LIKES:<br /><br />Like I said, I love the cover. It is really romantic and sets the mood for this lovely sequel. One of the biggest things I liked about this book was the plot. The first one was very different from what I've read. It was unique and flowed very well. This is one was no different. In fact, it was better than the first to me! Again, I loved the book in both POV's.I LOVED the concept of the Re Start program and the trip they went on, and the fat that Maggie and Caleb were once again reunited!!! It was, so wonderful and I fell in love even more with them!!<br /><br />We left off from Leaving Paradise where Caleb left Paradise again to go off by himself. His family never accepted him and he felt they were better off without him screwing everything up. His life fell apart the moment he was arrested for hitting Maggie with his car while driving home drunk. It was a really screwed up situation. But he got out of jail and did community service. He paid his dues. Then he and Maggie fell in love. She forgave him for everything, yet he wasn't convinced he was worthy of her or anyone else. So he left her and Paradise behind.<br /><br />The beginning of Return to Paradise, he gets in trouble again. He is staying in a drug house because he has nowhere to go and his roommate gets busted for drugs. He didn't sell or do any but still took the blame, almost ended up in the slammer for the 2nd time in 2 years. Until, Damon comes to his rescue.....AGAIN! I gotta say, this guy is a saint! That is where the Re Start program comes into play. He makes a deal with Caleb that if he goes with him to a camp for a few weeks telling his story to troubled kids about the consequences of drinking and driving , then he wont go to jail. So, he obliges not knowing he would see Maggie on the same trip. Things get tense, old wounds open up, and Hell breaks loose here and there. But it never ceases to impress me. The writing is beautiful, poignant and easy to follow. It flowed so amazingly. It was hard to put the book down. I did however, force myself because I knew if I kept reading I would have finished it in one day. It made me sad and depressed to know their sweet love story was coming to an end. <br /><br />I loved the new characters introduced in this book. My favorites were Lenny, although he annoyed me at the beginning but he totally got to me towards the end. I liked Trish, she was kind of a brat but I warmed up to her pretty quick. The rest of the characters were great. Lou was a great match for Maggie's mom. I was happy for them and for Maggie to actually have a father figure in her life! The whole concept was interesting and it made reading that much more fun. The witty and pissy banters between everyone was great! I laughed so much during most of Lenny's scenes, what a personality-sick and twisted but still pretty funny!<br /><br />The end was just amazing!! I was worried at first that things weren't going to turn out the way I hoped. But Simone didn't disappoint!!! I cried the last few chapters, it was romantic and sad but happy at the same time! I loved it through and through!<br /><br />DISLIKES:<br /><br />The only thing I didn't like was that it was too short!! I would have loved to see more of Maggie and Caleb's future eventhough it was clear what their future looked like! I guess I just wasn't to let go of these awesome characters that touched my heart all the way to my soul. They will always be in my heart though and I may just read this series over and over again!! I highly recommend this series to those that have ever wanted to give up on life. It shows everyone deserves second chances and to not ever give up but fight for what you want!! Thank you Caleb and Maggie for being so amazing!! And giving me this wonderful story of hope and love!!! FIVE STARS all the way!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15027354163472064786" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1857748934" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1857748934" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3399699-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386022874p2/3399699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1857748934?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/3399699-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=quick-read">quick-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=ya-quarterly-challenge-24-2017">ya-quarterly-challenge-24-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=multi-povs">multi-povs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=tough-subjects">tough-subjects</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1857748934" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6547123536655795557">My first official read of 2017 (though technically speaking I started this last year). My overall impression is that this narrative had some good points and some very bad points (keywords: rampant cliches and overly drawn out drama), but overall left a neutral impression on me. I think once the story got back to the main plot conflicts, I found a path to follow through the novel to the very end. Plus the audiobook narration was very good on the parts of Elizabeth Cottie as Maggie, and Nicholas M</span>
  <span id="freeText6547123536655795557" style="display:none">My first official read of 2017 (though technically speaking I started this last year). My overall impression is that this narrative had some good points and some very bad points (keywords: rampant cliches and overly drawn out drama), but overall left a neutral impression on me. I think once the story got back to the main plot conflicts, I found a path to follow through the novel to the very end. Plus the audiobook narration was very good on the parts of Elizabeth Cottie as Maggie, and Nicholas Mondetti as Caleb. <br /><br />"Return to Paradise" begins a little bit where "Leaving Paradise" left off, and finds Caleb and Maggie reuniting in a by-chance scenario. Caleb's gotten in trouble with the law again, and under his parole officer's wing, finds himself traveling with a group speaking to different kid/teen groups about how he ended up in prison/getting in trouble with the law and how it changed his life, in addition to having to stay at a campsite for a time. Conversely, Maggie travels with that same group talking about her experiences and how she ended up with her life-changing injuries. Suffice to say - Caleb and Maggie having to actively tell two sides of the same story is awkward and creates tension between them given their history. Caleb did a complete progress reversal of character of sorts since the last novel. He became worse for wear - being physically/mentally/emotionally abrasive - with Maggie being fully subjected to that abuse and lashing out. I hate romances like this, because it's like "Dude, Maggie was hurt because of circumstances that you were a part of, can you be more selfish and manipulative with your affection/possession/jealousy of her?"<br /><br />Ugh.<br /><br />I started following the narrative better after two things happened: 1. When the cat was let out of the bag with regards to the accident's events and 2. when the book actually got back to Paradise, with Caleb and Maggie both having to wrestle with how people in Paradise had changed since they'd been away. I appreciated the attention on the family conflicts and relationships, with a keen eye on the difficulties of starting over. Yet I almost feel like things in this novel were too easily resolved with respect to the central conflict in the way it was presented. Not that I couldn't believe that this could/would happen with both families having to come to terms with the truth of events, but it was the way it was presented. I found that I liked some of the supporting cast of characters in the book, but feel like they still primarily served as catalysts for the relationship between the protagonists of the novel.<br /><br />Overall, it's not one of my favorite series depicting this kind of subject matter with the romantic inclinations, but I was still able to appreciate parts of it.<br /><br />Overall score: 2.5/5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6547123536655795557" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_125247373" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125247373" />
    <a title="Crista" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3194546-crista"><img alt="Crista" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1284946251p2/3194546.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/125247373?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crista" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crista" href="/user/show/3194546-crista">Crista</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3194546-crista?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3194546-crista?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3194546-crista?shelf=bad-boys">bad-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3194546-crista?shelf=2-star">2-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125247373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3021405579310793705">After becoming accustomed to brilliance from this author, this one was really disappointing. <br/><br/>I think what bothers me most about this sequel to the amazing Leaving Paradise, is that I don't think the author stayed true to the characters. Caleb was simply awesome in Leaving Paradise. Yes he had issues and was angry, but never with Maggie. He treated her with kindness, concern, and respect the entire book. It was his attitude towards her that melted my heart and allowed me to care about his charact</span>
  <span id="freeText3021405579310793705" style="display:none">After becoming accustomed to brilliance from this author, this one was really disappointing. <br /><br />I think what bothers me most about this sequel to the amazing Leaving Paradise, is that I don't think the author stayed true to the characters. Caleb was simply awesome in Leaving Paradise. Yes he had issues and was angry, but never with Maggie. He treated her with kindness, concern, and respect the entire book. It was his attitude towards her that melted my heart and allowed me to care about his character. <br /><br />In Return to Paradise, both Maggie and Caleb's characters have changed so much that they are unrecognizable. Caleb is not a nice person for much of this book, even with Maggie. I found myself wondering who he was and wishing I could go back to the first book and remember him the way he was. Maggie is much stronger in this book, but I don't like the games she plays. One of the things I loved most about Maggie in the first book was her honesty and vulnerabiliy. In this book, she steps out of character many times and does things that really confused me. <br /><br />I wish I wouldn't have read this. It had some great moments so I give it 2 stars, but overall I think this book taints my feelings about the characters that I really loved from Leaving Paradise. I guess that's the risk you take when reading a sequel. Too bad Caleb and Maggie didn't get a more fitting one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3021405579310793705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6917862-booknut?shelf=can-t-get-enough-of">can-t-get-enough-of</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6917862-booknut?shelf=heartwarming">heartwarming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6917862-booknut?shelf=heartbreak-and-loss">heartbreak-and-loss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6917862-booknut?shelf=good-hearted-bad-boys">good-hearted-bad-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6917862-booknut?shelf=ethics-and-society">ethics-and-society</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer505961459" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4892366228967847317">I don't know what it says about my attention span, but the one thing I am hung up on in this book is the phrase in the last chapter that reads: "Please wait until the aircraft has come to a complete stop before deplaning."<br/><br/>Deplaning..is a word?! <br/><a target='_blank' title='ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting' href='http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/202/sensemuch.gif/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380405079ra/788689.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a target='_blank' href='http://imageshack.us' rel='nofollow noopener'></a><br/>According to the dictionary before me, 'deplaning' is: <br/> - a verb<br/> - means 'to disembark from an aircraft'<br/><br/>But apparently only awesome people in Simon Elkeles' world get to here their flight attendants say the word 'deplaning'. I have been on approximate</span>
  <span id="freeText4892366228967847317" style="display:none">I don't know what it says about my attention span, but the one thing I am hung up on in this book is the phrase in the last chapter that reads: "Please wait until the aircraft has come to a complete stop before deplaning."<br><br>Deplaning..is a word?! <br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/202/sensemuch.gif/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380405079ra/788689.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://imageshack.us" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br>According to the dictionary before me, 'deplaning' is: <br> - a verb<br> - means 'to disembark from an aircraft'<br><br>But apparently only awesome people in Simon Elkeles' world get to here their flight attendants say the word 'deplaning'. I have been on approximately 14 airplane trips in my life and on NONE of them has anyone been cool enough to use fancy lingo. It's always "before exiting the aircraft", "disembarking" or "before getting off". Nice. Really snazzy. I feel SO loved.<br><br>Deplaning just sounds so...so...slick. And cool. And now I am going to stop obsessing over that one word and get onto obsessing over the cute mess that is Caleb and Maggie.<br><br>At first, all I wanted to do was punch Caleb's annoying (hot...mesmerising...chiselled...) face. Because heeeeeeeeello ladies - this dude is a heartbreaker! He deserted her! Yeah, he had good reasons (NB: in his head) but dude:<br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/835/tumblrlx13l6nrdr1qzhvg4.gif/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380405079ra/788690.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br> <a target="_blank" href="http://imageshack.us" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br>And that is NOT okay. *stares Caleb down*<br><br>But Maggie gets him back. They get stuck together in this program called ReSTART (I don't know why they capitalise the START and not the RE since the whole point is that they're REstarting their lives and helping others to do so, but anyways...) where people share their drink driving/stupid driving experiences with others youths around the country. <br><br>Kudos to Maggie for finding a way to get back at Caleb for dumping her in the lake for his own amusement. What does she do? Well, when he starts staring into her eyes, thinking about kissing her, she pretends she's going to...and then gets out and leaves him. Wanting her. Alone. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380405079ra/788691.gif" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>And yeah, Caleb's hot. But the one thing I H-A-T-E about him is his piggish, bullheaded attitude issues. Give. The girl. A break. You're a rollercoaster, dude, and you expect her to keep up with your mood swings?! That's a psychiatrist's job. Or your parents'. She loves you and you just treat her like dirt but expect her to wait for you like the horrible (hot...swoon-worthy...) jerk you are. <br><br>Shame. On. You!<br><br>So it shouldn't be much of a spoiler if I tell you all that:<br>1.) They kiss at least once in this book<br>2.) You do get to 'see' Caleb shirtless (always a bonus)<br>3.) There will be a 'crying I can't stand you leave me the hell alone' scene<br>4.) Shit will go down<br>5.) True love will conquer all (*sings* "LOVE LIFTS US UP WHERE WE BELONG!" (sorry, couldn't help it!!))<br>6.) Drink driving is condemned. Duh. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4892366228967847317" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/121258809" />
    <a title="Nomes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3842653-nomes"><img alt="Nomes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499148999p2/3842653.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/121258809?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nomes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nomes" href="/user/show/3842653-nomes">Nomes</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=i-thought-i-would-love-this-but">i-thought-i-would-love-this-but</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=alternating-m-f-pov">alternating-m-f-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=out-of-the-loop">out-of-the-loop</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=not-for-me">not-for-me</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer121258809" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14603617107935343987">1.5 stars<br/><br/>Honestly, I just didn't get what the point of this book was?<br/><br/>Really - why did there need to be a sequel when it had no strong plot? I would've preferred to just leave it at the first book without the last chapter that lead into a sequel.<br/><br/>I loved caleb in the first one - but in this I just didnt get him and his motivations at all. seemed contrived for the sake of drama. And despite being inside his head for most of the book - I still didn't get why he behaved how he did towards Maggie and </span>
  <span id="freeText14603617107935343987" style="display:none">1.5 stars<br /><br />Honestly, I just didn't get what the point of this book was?<br /><br />Really - why did there need to be a sequel when it had no strong plot? I would've preferred to just leave it at the first book without the last chapter that lead into a sequel.<br /><br />I loved caleb in the first one - but in this I just didnt get him and his motivations at all. seemed contrived for the sake of drama. And despite being inside his head for most of the book - I still didn't get why he behaved how he did towards Maggie and I started not liking him and then at some point I really stopped caring about him (and Maggie), which was very disappointing as the reason I was so looking forward to this sequel was because of how invested I was in Caleb.<br /><br />The plot meandered along relying on dragging out Caleb's attitudes/angst and Maggie's stubbornness. It felt like it was flailing around and often side-plots seemed thrown in to create drama rather than remaining true to the characters motivations. <br /><br />A combination of the lack of tension and stakes that weren't continually raised and no strong premise to suck me in - meant other things I'd normally overlook started to bug me - the dialogue and cliffhanger chapter endings grated. The swearing and crude jokes did not humour me.<br /><br />The teens who were from broken and rough backgrounds felt gimmicky and caricatured and unbelievable - even contrived to illustrate some kind of point? <br /><br />Also, I loved the sexual tension in the first title but here I felt none of that at all.<br /><br />I don't normally write detailed reviews for books that bombed out for me but I really feel disappointed with this title especially after loving the first one and recommending it to many reader friends. The first one had a great premise and twists and awesome stakes that were continually raised and the characters felt genuine. I was expecting a lot more from this and it surprised me how poorly written it was which makes me wonder if the first book was too but I overlooked it as the story sucked me in?<br /><br />Unfortunately after reading this I am doubtful I will feel compelled to pick up another book by Elkeles. After this, I can say it's not really my kind of book - too melodramatic and soap-ish. <br /><br />(although readers who are into drama and romance and angst may find something here to enjoy).<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14603617107935343987" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer646872483900235047">A complete and utter travesty. 1.5 stars. Now, i'm not one to dislike books due to mature content, but I felt as if the only real purpose of this book was to let us all know how much Caleb and Maggie wanted to get into eachothers pants. Completley rushed, unnecessary characters and plot events were major problems and, to top it off, we had a constant ridiculous battle between the two - 'I love you', 'we can't be together','let's just have a quick snog before we go back to biting eachothers heads</span>
  <span id="freeText646872483900235047" style="display:none">A complete and utter travesty. 1.5 stars. Now, i'm not one to dislike books due to mature content, but I felt as if the only real purpose of this book was to let us all know how much Caleb and Maggie wanted to get into eachothers pants. Completley rushed, unnecessary characters and plot events were major problems and, to top it off, we had a constant ridiculous battle between the two - 'I love you', 'we can't be together','let's just have a quick snog before we go back to biting eachothers heads off'...<br /><br />I am a huge fan of Simone Elkeles, with Perfect Chemistry being one of my favorite reads of 2010! When I read Leaving Paradise, it was a little different in tone but still retained that certain charm which I had come to love about Elkeles' writing. However, this book seemed as if it was written as a weak fan fiction. Both Caleb and Maggie were out of character and were, to be totally honest, infuriating.<br /><br />BUT, (and a big but at that), the book wasn't all that horrific. There were funny elements to the book and some scenes did hold a certain shock-value, but as a whole, this book was thoroughly dissapointing and this is said by someone who had little-no expectations for the books events.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer94647904" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16812168815458263218">For fans of Leaving Paradise that wished for an alternate ending, <b>Return to Paradise</b> is a must read. This second and hopefully final installment provided the ending that I felt Maggie and Caleb deserved in the first book. <br/><br/>There were parts of the story that felt a bit contrived, but despite the rough patches in this book, I really enjoyed it. The HEA did take a scenic route with poor moves and actions by both main characters, but in the end, it all came together quite nicely. <br/><br/>The book does contai</span>
  <span id="freeText16812168815458263218" style="display:none">For fans of Leaving Paradise that wished for an alternate ending, <b>Return to Paradise</b> is a must read. This second and hopefully final installment provided the ending that I felt Maggie and Caleb deserved in the first book. <br /><br />There were parts of the story that felt a bit contrived, but despite the rough patches in this book, I really enjoyed it. The HEA did take a scenic route with poor moves and actions by both main characters, but in the end, it all came together quite nicely. <br /><br />The book does contain a healthy dose of <i>f bombs</i>, which caught me a little off guard, only because I wasn’t expecting it from Elkeles, but it never really put me off. Either way, it was great to revisit Paradise with Maggie and Caleb eight months after the last book left off, and most of all it was great to meet a new set of secondary characters that made the story engaging and humorous, including <i>loyal</i> Matt, <i>funny</i> Lenny, <i>sad</i> Erin, and <i>angry</i> Trish.<br /><br />The ending was spot on, the back-stories of some of the characters were full of depth and this book completed my journey with these characters in a way the first book never really achieved. I enjoyed it much!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16812168815458263218" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Love is a mutual respect for one another, something you and I don't have. <br/><br/><b>For Caleb, LOVE is. . . </b><br/>Love isn't about honesty. It's about protecting the people you love from things that will hurt them. That's love.<br/><br/>I really enjoy myself reading this. <div id="review_162244989" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/162244989" />
    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/162244989?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=poc">poc</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer162244989" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9414782061082366328">I think Gayle Forman has ruined all other realistic YA fiction for me. I liked <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/544424.Leaving_Paradise__Leaving_Paradise___1_' title='Leaving Paradise (Leaving Paradise, #1) by Simone Elkeles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Leaving Paradise</a> well enough, because the idea of a girl forgiving a boy who hit her with a car is an interesting set-up...but after reading such beautiful, emotional books as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4374400.If_I_Stay__If_I_Stay___1_' title='If I Stay (If I Stay, #1) by Gayle Forman' rel='nofollow noopener'>If I Stay</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8492825.Where_She_Went__If_I_Stay___2_' title='Where She Went (If I Stay, #2) by Gayle Forman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Where She Went</a>, Simone Elkeles' work feels fairly contrived and lacking in depth. A lot of this book just didn't make any sense to me, either--<i>what</i> kind of camp is this exactly where Caleb and Maggie are forced to be together? Wher</span>
  <span id="freeText9414782061082366328" style="display:none">I think Gayle Forman has ruined all other realistic YA fiction for me. I liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/544424.Leaving_Paradise__Leaving_Paradise___1_" title="Leaving Paradise (Leaving Paradise, #1) by Simone Elkeles" rel="nofollow noopener">Leaving Paradise</a> well enough, because the idea of a girl forgiving a boy who hit her with a car is an interesting set-up...but after reading such beautiful, emotional books as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4374400.If_I_Stay__If_I_Stay___1_" title="If I Stay (If I Stay, #1) by Gayle Forman" rel="nofollow noopener">If I Stay</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8492825.Where_She_Went__If_I_Stay___2_" title="Where She Went (If I Stay, #2) by Gayle Forman" rel="nofollow noopener">Where She Went</a>, Simone Elkeles' work feels fairly contrived and lacking in depth. A lot of this book just didn't make any sense to me, either--<i>what</i> kind of camp is this exactly where Caleb and Maggie are forced to be together? Where the cabins and bathrooms are co-ed and the entire program is just six kids and one counselor who also happens to be Caleb's transition counselor? It's all just too weird and unrealistic.<br /><br />The relationship between the two characters is not shallow, exactly, but it's just not all that interesting either. It's probably not fair to read most books after experiencing the genuine depth and connection between the characters in Gayle Forman's books (even the secondary ones), but it's hard not to wish that other novels with similar subjects came even close to eliciting the same level of gut-wrenching response. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9414782061082366328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer91976458" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer6442411100803577334">I feel so much better now that I've read this book. I loved the first one but I was annoyed that we didn't get the closure that was very much needed.<br/>This, was much better.<br/>Caleb and Maggie never had the ideal relationship to begin with and things aren't looking to good when these two meet up again eight months later.<br/>Feelings are hurt-repeatedly, Games are played-repeated and I really wanted to knock these two heads together-repeatedly.<br/><br/>Caleb, at first was pretty much your standard jerk with an ext</span>
  <span id="freeText6442411100803577334" style="display:none">I feel so much better now that I've read this book. I loved the first one but I was annoyed that we didn't get the closure that was very much needed.<br />This, was much better.<br />Caleb and Maggie never had the ideal relationship to begin with and things aren't looking to good when these two meet up again eight months later.<br />Feelings are hurt-repeatedly, Games are played-repeated and I really wanted to knock these two heads together-repeatedly.<br /><br />Caleb, at first was pretty much your standard jerk with an extra side of attitude just for kicks, the boy has issues. Maggie isn't any better and she was borderline irritating.<br />At one point or another, both of them pissed me off, I wanted to slap Caleb and I couldn't believe Maggie went <i>there</i>.<br />Lots of drama, lots of angst but we also got a whole lotta smiles.<br /> <br />Simone Elkeles style continues to impress and amaze me. The women knows how to write and can really deliver high strung emotions to a seemingly impossible situation. Her books are always an eager must read then gone to fast. It's never enough and I always seem to want more.<br /><br />Basically I just loved this book, I loved the new faces we meet, I love Caleb and Maggie and think they have such a wonderfully unique bond that just makes my insides want to gush. <br />Through trust and truth we finally get an ending that was long past due and so worth the wait.<br />Heartwarming and honest, <b>Return to Paradise</b> and fall in love with Caleb and Maggie all over again! </span>

<div id="review_106460393" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/106460393" />
    <a title="Angie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50378-angie"><img alt="Angie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510342996p2/50378.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/106460393?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angie" href="/user/show/50378-angie">Angie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=absolute-train-wreck">absolute-train-wreck</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer106460393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3612669021059708494">I was so happily surprised (and intensely affected) by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/544424.Leaving_Paradise__Leaving_Paradise___1_' title='Leaving Paradise (Leaving Paradise, #1) by Simone Elkeles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Leaving Paradise</a> that I couldn't wait to start in on the sequel, the inevitably titled RETURN TO PARADISE. Honestly, I loved Maggie and Caleb so much that I savored the thought of them back on the page together, dealing with the awkward and ambiguous place they were unceremoniously left in at the end of the first book. Naturally, snagging an ARC of RETURN TO PARADISE was pretty high up on my list of things to do at BEA. And I hadn't even rea</span>
  <span id="freeText3612669021059708494" style="display:none">I was so happily surprised (and intensely affected) by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/544424.Leaving_Paradise__Leaving_Paradise___1_" title="Leaving Paradise (Leaving Paradise, #1) by Simone Elkeles" rel="nofollow noopener">Leaving Paradise</a> that I couldn't wait to start in on the sequel, the inevitably titled RETURN TO PARADISE. Honestly, I loved Maggie and Caleb so much that I savored the thought of them back on the page together, dealing with the awkward and ambiguous place they were unceremoniously left in at the end of the first book. Naturally, snagging an ARC of RETURN TO PARADISE was pretty high up on my list of things to do at BEA. And I hadn't even read the first book yet! I have to say I'm not loving the cover, though. The newer cover of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/544424.Leaving_Paradise__Leaving_Paradise___1_" title="Leaving Paradise (Leaving Paradise, #1) by Simone Elkeles" rel="nofollow noopener">Leaving Paradise</a> struck just the right note, when it comes to the fear and pain and connection between these two characters. The cover of the sequel just doesn't measure up, in my opinion. It probably doesn't help that that's not how I picture either of them and that kissing under the moonlight by a lake (while it may happen in the book) just doesn't really encompass the whole of what's going on in this story. But enough about that. On to the insides.<br /><br />Maggie has worked for eight grueling months to put Caleb Becker and his inexplicable desertion behind her. She's gone over and over it in her mind and come to the conclusion that if he wasn't willing to tough it out and <i>stay</i> and fight to keep what was between them alive, then she's not going to waste her life crying over the loss. And she's doing a fine job of moving on. Getting ready to leave for Spain on study abroad, Maggie is spending her summer participating in a teen outreach program wherein she travels with a group of other kids whose lives were altered by substance abuse or violence or unutterably bad decisions, giving talks to other teens who might be on the verge of trouble. Unfortunately, Maggie's resolve is put to the test when Caleb abruptly joins the group. Dragged back from wherever he'd disappeared to by his former transition counselor Damon, this trip is Caleb's last chance to redeem himself and avoid being sent back to jail for living with drug dealers for the last several months. Against their better judgement, Maggie and Caleb set out on the venture, unwilling and unhappy trip mates. Of course there are a few other misfits along for the ride and their stories get interwoven with this one, but the focus remains on the emotional damage these two have undergone in the last year and the large chasm that has cropped up between them when once they were so close.<br /><br />I don't really know how to put this. But this book was a very big disappointment. Where the first was such a wonderfully absorbing surprise, this one meandered on and on until I had to force myself to finish it. The writing was simply not up to par with that of her previous books and this was one instance of the uncorrected mistakes in the ARC frequently distracting me. I realize these will be corrected in the final version. But the main problem I had with it were actually the odd changes in the two principal characters. Caleb was rough in the first book. As a direct result of spending a year in juvie, he was necessarily changed by the experience. But he was never mean. Coarse and frustrated and full to the brim with anger, yes. But never mean. In an unpleasantly snarky way. And certainly not to Maggie. That hesitant reserve he had when it came to her was such a highlight for me. But in RETURN TO PARADISE, he is mean. Downright lousy sometimes. I didn't buy it, I didn't like it, and it was painful to read not only because of how it affected the other characters but because it felt inauthentic to me as the reader. Maggie was vulnerable and afraid in the first book. As a direct result of the accident that left her maimed, she was understandably that way. And she does grow a spine in this book. Or at least we're to believe she has. But she seems to waffle back and forth all over the place when it comes to taking what Caleb deals her and that, too, felt wrong to me somehow. These two knew each other better than that. Their connection was real and fine and worth reading about before. And I know there needs to be conflict and tension to provide fodder for a sequel at all, but it just came off as messy and immature here. Which is such a shame, as I truly missed that breathtaking, organic connection from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/544424.Leaving_Paradise__Leaving_Paradise___1_" title="Leaving Paradise (Leaving Paradise, #1) by Simone Elkeles" rel="nofollow noopener">Leaving Paradise</a>. So definitely don't miss the first book. But unfortunately I'd recommend giving this one a pass and just imagining up the ending you'd like in your head instead.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3612669021059708494" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_174820307" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/174820307" />
    <a title="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3024878-donna-book-passion-for-life"><img alt="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563622982p2/3024878.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/174820307?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" href="/user/show/3024878-donna-book-passion-for-life">Donna {Book Passion For Life}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024878-donna-book-passion-for-life?shelf=ya-contemporary-romance">ya-contemporary-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer174820307" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer680686621599945917">Posted on: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://bookpassionforlife.blogspot.com'>http://bookpassionforlife.blogspot.com</a><br/><br/>After finishing Leaving Paradise I was so excited to start this book…. I headed for it straight away. I was really worried that I would be disappointed with it, just because I’d hear a few negative reviews but it’s safe to say……Simone Elkeles has done it again and completely blown me away again. Wow! Just wow! <br/><br/>Return to Paradise starts 8 months later meeting Caleb in trouble. When he’s been arrested and faces jail time, Caleb has known one else to</span>
  <span id="freeText680686621599945917" style="display:none">Posted on: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bookpassionforlife.blogspot.com">http://bookpassionforlife.blogspot.com</a><br /><br />After finishing Leaving Paradise I was so excited to start this book…. I headed for it straight away. I was really worried that I would be disappointed with it, just because I’d hear a few negative reviews but it’s safe to say……Simone Elkeles has done it again and completely blown me away again. Wow! Just wow! <br /><br />Return to Paradise starts 8 months later meeting Caleb in trouble. When he’s been arrested and faces jail time, Caleb has known one else to turn to but his former mentor Damon. Damon can get him out of trouble providing Caleb joins a Re-Start Programme for kids affected by drunk driving. The morning of the trip Caleb finds himself face to face with Maggie…..who is also taking part in the programme. Thinking everything will be fine, both Caleb and Maggie fight their attraction for one another and both wishing they could finally reveal what really happened on the night of the crash. <br /><br />I honestly have to say wow again! Honestly, wow! I thought the first book was fantastic but this was a completely different read. I’ve never been more on edge while reading a book; I just couldn’t keep my excitement in. You’re thrown into the lives of Caleb and Maggie from the first page and the passion of their relationship is just completely undeniable once again.<br /><br />We get to see a whole new different side to both of the characters. They’ve both grown over the 8 months they been apart but they’ve both become stronger…Maggie especially. She finally comes out of the shell she has been living in since the accident and after losing Caleb, she finally starts trying to live her life with no regrets and really try to be a different person. Now Caleb…he’s had a hard time during the 8 months apart but my god, I’ve never meet anyone more stubborn all my life. I did sometimes want to give him a good shake but I’m glad he finally came to terms with everything that had happened since the accident. He did grow as a character by the end of the book and I loved that we got to see a different side to him. <br /><br />I also really enjoyed the new characters that were introduced even though they were all battling their own problems, they all came together and were funny, caring and so much fun to read about. I loved that Simone managed to bring some of them back to Paradise and created a happy ending for them as she could of. <br /><br />Overall, not only has Simone managed to write a fantastic sequel but she has managed to pack this story with even more emotion, more passion and more intense scenes that will leave the reader dying to finish the book. A fantastic end to a fantastic series and one I know I will read over and over again. Highly recommended to all. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="680686621599945917" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98209145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9535460292191526505">This is an outstanding sequel to LEAVING PARADISE! I couldn't put this book down. I rarely would describe a novel as exquisite, but it fits. Once again, Simone Elkeles draws the reader in by alternating between Caleb and Maggie's narration, and it works beautifully.<br/>RETURN TO PARADISE is a richly written, emotionally charged novel that will leave you satisfied, but also wishing that the last page didn't come so quickly. <br/>What makes Simone Elkeles's books (including this one) so fabulous is the rea</span>
  <span id="freeText9535460292191526505" style="display:none">This is an outstanding sequel to LEAVING PARADISE! I couldn't put this book down. I rarely would describe a novel as exquisite, but it fits. Once again, Simone Elkeles draws the reader in by alternating between Caleb and Maggie's narration, and it works beautifully.<br />RETURN TO PARADISE is a richly written, emotionally charged novel that will leave you satisfied, but also wishing that the last page didn't come so quickly. <br />What makes Simone Elkeles's books (including this one) so fabulous is the realistic portrayal of characters from all different life experiences. She doesn't shy away from the tough issues that teens face today. She seamlessly integrates sexuality, disabilities, race, religion and faith, love, family dynamics, drug use, and divorce. All of Simone Elkeles's main characters face difficult challenges and Caleb and Maggie are no exception. There is no sugar coating life, but love can make a person better, can help to overcome obstacles, and can give strength when you're feeling weak.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9535460292191526505" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_121446383" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <a title="Peep (Pop! Pop!)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Peep (Pop! Pop!)" href="/user/show/2507910-peep-pop-pop">Peep (Pop! Pop!)</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2507910-peep-pop-pop?shelf=so-not-impressed">so-not-impressed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2507910-peep-pop-pop?shelf=addicted-to-ya">addicted-to-ya</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer121446383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14751232818516662772">I gotta admit that I really wanted to like this one. Now we all know that Simone Elkeles can write some really good cheese and like any crazy person, I tend to like her cheese. I really, really liked Leaving Paradise. It drew me and had me floored. Return to Paradise didn't really do anything but bore me... and I didn't even want it to be that way! We get treated to lines like:<br/><br/><blockquote>If he doesn't come back to you, he wasn't yours to begin with.</blockquote><br/><br/>I swear to you I am not kidding! Yes, that line? That is s</span>
  <span id="freeText14751232818516662772" style="display:none">I gotta admit that I really wanted to like this one. Now we all know that Simone Elkeles can write some really good cheese and like any crazy person, I tend to like her cheese. I really, really liked Leaving Paradise. It drew me and had me floored. Return to Paradise didn't really do anything but bore me... and I didn't even want it to be that way! We get treated to lines like:<br /><br /><blockquote>If he doesn't come back to you, he wasn't yours to begin with.</blockquote><br /><br />I swear to you I am not kidding! Yes, that line? That is so not cool and made me groan (LOUDLY) when I read it. Really? That's the best line you could come up with Maggie? I would have laughed in her face if she'd said it to me!<br /><br />Return to Paradise starts about 8 months after Caleb left Paradise. I think he should have waited a little longer to return because maybe then the book would have been better??? I don't know. <br /><br />Caleb was well, mean. He was moody and kind of violent. I guess holding all that in for so long would make you get like that, but we didn't really get to see the transition. It was like awesome, tortured Caleb in the first book and moody, mean Caleb in book 2. Nothing to show us why, after all this time, he became so mean. I missed the charm from the first book. <br /><br />I still liked Maggie though. She was still sweet and much tougher than the first time around. I liked the addition of the new characters. Lenny was awful joke kind of funny, but I still liked him. <br /><br />Some of the things felt really contrived, like how Caleb ended up seeing Maggie again. Also, the juvie scenes just seemed so, well, scripted - just not believable.<br /><br />I loved the cover on the first book but this one seemed amateur, don't you think? I was even disappointed in the epilogue! And that's usually my favorite kind of cheese! It felt like she just turned the last chapter into an epilogue, rather than making an epilogue of EPIC proportions... and I missed that. I wanted to be wowed by the future but instead I got a measly one year later. Wait, it wasn't even a year. Tsk, tsk, tsk. I feel cheated. Maybe there will be a third book? To talk about some of the new character introduced? But I guess we kind of know how their story works out, huh?<br /><br />So, would I recommend this one? Probably not. I was fairly disappointed in it as you can tell. Like most of her books, it's definitely for older teens based on the content. I didn't hate this one, but I didn't like it either. Would I read her next book? You betcha! I still like what Simone's doing!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14751232818516662772" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_110270848" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/110270848" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3333280-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1266944727p2/3333280.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/110270848?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/3333280-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Teens; Elkeles fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Tatiana by: </span>
      Jackie from Goodreads
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3333280-tatiana?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3333280-tatiana?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3333280-tatiana?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3333280-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3333280-tatiana?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110270848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11506194801352277359">This was a roller coaster story that immediately picks up eight months later from when Caleb disappeared from Maggie's life, never once contacting her, his family or friends in all that time. And now - he's back.<br/><br/>SPOILER ALERT!!!<br/><br/>Caleb is barely living his life legally in Chicago, holding down a menial job by day, and sleeping in a drug den by night, not able to sleep and chase away his personal demons, and he cannot get Maggie out of his mind. Although Caleb has nothing to do with his roommates i</span>
  <span id="freeText11506194801352277359" style="display:none">This was a roller coaster story that immediately picks up eight months later from when Caleb disappeared from Maggie's life, never once contacting her, his family or friends in all that time. And now - he's back.<br /><br />SPOILER ALERT!!!<br /><br />Caleb is barely living his life legally in Chicago, holding down a menial job by day, and sleeping in a drug den by night, not able to sleep and chase away his personal demons, and he cannot get Maggie out of his mind. Although Caleb has nothing to do with his roommates illegal activities, he is taken to the police station when the house is raided. The next thing Caleb knows, he can either face charges, or lean on his former counselor, hard-as-nails Damon. Suddenly, Caleb is on Damon's time, and has to enter a one-month program to stay out of jail, and special program that throws victims and perpetrators of reckless and drunken driving together. Their collective purpose? To take a tour of different facilities and warn at-risk youth to not go down the path they did, or to witness the consequences of rash actions. Of course, Maggie is in this program in order to secure her one-year scholarship to Spain, and she is a stronger and more resilient woman who will not leave just because her wannabe boyfriend showed up out of nowhere. What makes this book more human are the salty cast of misfits that are thrown together for the month, kids who are so messed up for a variety of reasons, and slowly share their harrowing stories with each other, putting Caleb and Maggie's sordid problems into perspective. But the elephant in the room is truth and honesty, something these two have a hard time dabbling in. We already know that Caleb is innocent and it was his twin sister Leah, Maggie's best friend, that crippled Maggie in that drunken accident. But Maggie won't tell Caleb she knows the truth, and Caleb is tormenting himself with telling Maggie what really happened, wondering if his promise to Leah to take this dark secret to his grave is worth all he has lost and is poised to lose if he doesn't come clean.<br /><br />Needless to say, I enjoyed the book thoroughly, and I highly recommend it for teens 9th grade and up. Although there is still no sex (sorry Caleb fans!), there are sexual situations. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11506194801352277359" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_126270039" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/126270039" />
    <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip"><img alt="Jennifer Wardrip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442657515p2/1125613.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/126270039?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Wardrip" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip">Jennifer Wardrip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=read-by-other-reviewers">read-by-other-reviewers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=trt-posted-reviews">trt-posted-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer126270039" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11772328596458445985">Reviewed by Randstostipher "tallnlankyrn" Nguyen for TeensReadToo.com<br/><br/>Leaving Paradise, Caleb Becker thought he would have a better life, even if it meant letting go of Maggie. Yet Caleb still finds himself in trouble, once again not being his fault. With the departure of Caleb, Maggie Armstrong waited and waited for his return. As the days went by, the chances of reuniting with Caleb seemed non-existent. So Maggie decided that she would become stronger, to become more independent.<br/><br/>As if fate had </span>
  <span id="freeText11772328596458445985" style="display:none">Reviewed by Randstostipher "tallnlankyrn" Nguyen for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />Leaving Paradise, Caleb Becker thought he would have a better life, even if it meant letting go of Maggie. Yet Caleb still finds himself in trouble, once again not being his fault. With the departure of Caleb, Maggie Armstrong waited and waited for his return. As the days went by, the chances of reuniting with Caleb seemed non-existent. So Maggie decided that she would become stronger, to become more independent.<br /><br />As if fate had another plan for them, Caleb and Maggie are reunited with the help of the Re-START program. The program that will keep Caleb from going to jail again and will help Maggie cope. During the four-week trip, Maggie and Caleb and four other teens drive around, talking to others about the accidents that they may have caused or experienced firsthand.<br /><br />As the trip continues, emotions and feelings between Caleb and Maggie arise once again, creating conflicts, confusion, and breakdowns. Maggie knows the truth about the accident and all she wants is for Caleb to tell her himself. But Caleb is not aware that Maggie already knows, and doesn't want to break his promise to his sister.<br /><br />In the end, the only way to make their relationship stronger is for Caleb to return to Paradise, where he will ultimately resolve the issues surrounding the accident, including those dealing with his family. However, doing so could have a negative outcome for his sister. Is Caleb willing to take the risk in order to finally develop a lasting relationship with Maggie, or will his promise to his sister mean more?<br /><br />Once again, Simone Elkeles geniusly writes a sequel that allows the reader to fall in love all over again with her characters. Maggie and Caleb are unquestionably the strongest, and of course cutest, characters and continue to be throughout the story as they both push each other because they know it is for the best. The addition of lovable characters such as Lenny and Julio adds another dynamic to the novel that makes it even more enjoyable.<br /><br />RETURN TO PARADISE will not disappoint readers who enjoyed LEAVING PARADISE. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11772328596458445985" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/271491739" />
    <a title="Sarah Marie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6515737-sarah-marie"><img alt="Sarah Marie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589089368p2/6515737.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/271491739?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Marie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Marie" href="/user/show/6515737-sarah-marie">Sarah Marie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=lol-i-love-books-that-make-me-laugh">lol-i-love-books-that-make-me-laugh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=can-i-have-your-babies">can-i-have-your-babies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer271491739" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10951181366312529976"><u>Return to Paradise</u> by Simone Elkeles<br/><br/>Second in the Leaving Paradise series<br/><br/><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/><p>Return to Paradise picks up eight months after Leaving Paradise. Vowing to keep a secret that could destroy everything if the truth got out, Caleb Becker left Paradise eight months ago and left the he loved, Maggie Armstrong. Now Caleb is in trouble and he has a choice to either participate in the Re-START program or go to prison. Maggie’s tried to forget about Caleb, but when they are forced to participate in RE-S</p></span>
  <span id="freeText10951181366312529976" style="display:none"><u>Return to Paradise</u> by Simone Elkeles<br><br>Second in the Leaving Paradise series<br><br><b>3.5 stars</b><br><br><p>Return to Paradise picks up eight months after Leaving Paradise. Vowing to keep a secret that could destroy everything if the truth got out, Caleb Becker left Paradise eight months ago and left the he loved, Maggie Armstrong. Now Caleb is in trouble and he has a choice to either participate in the Re-START program or go to prison. Maggie’s tried to forget about Caleb, but when they are forced to participate in RE-START together, the old feelings she tried so hard to forget about come back. Return to Paradise was as good as Leaving Paradise, but I also felt like I needed more and the epilogue could’ve brought more to the table. It’s hard to explain the empty, unsatisfied feeling I had after reading this novel. I think it had something to do with the fact that this was last I would see of Caleb and Maggie.</p><br><br><b>Whimsical Writing Scale: 3.75</b><br><br><p>The main female character is again Maggie. I liked her as much as I liked her the last time.</p><br><b>Kick-Butt Heroine Scale: 4.25</b><br><br><p>The main male character is again Caleb. I didn’t like him as much as I liked him in Leaving Paradise because he kept being a huge jerk to Maggie. The whole time I kept thinking stop being a jerk to her and just tell her you love her. Gosh sometimes the boys in YA can be so frustrating.</p><br><br><b>Swoon Worthy Scale: 3</b><br><br><p><b>The Villain</b>- There was no real villain in this book, except Caleb‘s jerkiness/protectiveness and Maggie’s reluctance.<br><b>Villain Scale: NO REAL VILLAIN</b><br>Lenny was the best character in the novel hands down.</p><br><b>Character Scale: 4.25</b><br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/crying%20gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380356441ra/708054.gif" alt="crying gif Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Plotastic Scale: 3</b><br><br><b>Cover Thoughts: I don’t really like this cover. I’m not impressed with artwork and it was a letdown to look at it.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10951181366312529976" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
