<div id="review_109769590" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/109769590" />
    <a title="Courtney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030363-courtney"><img alt="Courtney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476724853p2/3030363.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/109769590?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Courtney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Courtney" href="/user/show/3030363-courtney">Courtney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer109769590" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8064375054203205476">Can I just let out my emotions real quick? Okay, thanks.<br/>OHMYGOSHOHMYGOSHOHMYGOSHOHMYGOSHOHMYGOSHOHMYGOSH.<br/>OH. MY. GOSH.<br/>Okay. Breathe, Courtney.<br/><br/>Simone Elkeles has done it ONCE AGAIN! I read Leaving Paradise after Perfect Chemistry some months back. I remember thinking how much I enjoyed Simone's writing style.<br/>It was very different from other stories I have read. And for that, I was grateful.<br/>None of that long, drawn out descriptions. Simone kept the story going with real language anyone can relate </span>
  <span id="freeText8064375054203205476" style="display:none">Can I just let out my emotions real quick? Okay, thanks.<br />OHMYGOSHOHMYGOSHOHMYGOSHOHMYGOSHOHMYGOSHOHMYGOSH.<br />OH. MY. GOSH.<br />Okay. Breathe, Courtney.<br /><br />Simone Elkeles has done it ONCE AGAIN! I read Leaving Paradise after Perfect Chemistry some months back. I remember thinking how much I enjoyed Simone's writing style.<br />It was very different from other stories I have read. And for that, I was grateful.<br />None of that long, drawn out descriptions. Simone kept the story going with real language anyone can relate to.<br />Return To Paradise didn't change my opinion. Actually, it made it better, if that is even possible.<br />When you start RTP, you jump right back into Caleb Becker and Maggie Armstrong's worlds.<br /><br />Caleb hasn't been back to Paradise for 8 months. Hasn't talked to family, friends, not even Maggie.<br />Maggie has been trying to hold herself together these past 8 months without Caleb. She always had hope he would come back. But he never did.<br />Now, due to unfortunate circumstances, they are back in the same town. In the same van, even.<br />From the moment they lay eyes on each other, you are holding your breath and yelling at the pages "KISS ALREADY!".<br />The tension between Caleb and Maggie is thick and I love it! They are perfect together, especially when they fight!<br />The back story on all the characters are amazing. Some of the minor characters will really get to you in a very good way.<br /><br />My head is going a million mph. And I know if I keep rambling, I will spill about the entire book. So, I'll leave my review to: I absolutely loved it!<br /><br />Now, onto the cover. I'm not too excited about it. This is just the ARC cover, so it can change between now and publication date. And, honestly, I hope it does.<br />The Return To Paradise ARC cover doesn't grab my attention like Simone Elkeles' other novels did.<br /><br />But other than my dislike for the cover, Return To Paradise is a must read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8064375054203205476" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JlRAx9wDo7PSSgJHHBOp8yYFw8L4MnBYd0hhro7Z230vdpDLkxiry4rhi+wHvSQ3mgi/D5gIKZfCrDhCbInq1w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('aT3tdSOD/zIzplP1ByiZfyP7pA+S1BVvXDxQLjGnNARgHz15bJj3SmsN2l4chhS7n/bYwvLuTKDp2AnC0/cFrg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13260010924057501622">Simone Elkeles is a <i>New York Times</i> and <i>USA Today</i> bestselling author of novels for teens. Simone’s books have won many awards including being YALSA Top Ten Quick Picks for Reluctant Young Adult Readers, being named to the YALSA Popular Paperbacks and Teens Top Ten lists, and added to the Illinois “Read for a Lifetime” Reading List. Simone also won the coveted RITA award from the Romance Writers of </span>
  <span id="freeText13260010924057501622" style="display:none">Simone Elkeles is a <i>New York Times</i> and <i>USA Today</i> bestselling author of novels for teens. Simone’s books have won many awards including being YALSA Top Ten Quick Picks for Reluctant Young Adult Readers, being named to the YALSA Popular Paperbacks and Teens Top Ten lists, and added to the Illinois “Read for a Lifetime” Reading List. Simone also won the coveted RITA award from the Romance Writers of America for her book Perfect Chemistry. Simone is especially proud of the fact that the Illinois Association of Teachers of English named her Author of the Year. <br /><br />Simone was born and raised in the suburbs of Chicago, where she still lives today. Simone went to the University of Illinois in Urbana-Champaign and received her Bachelor’s of Science there in Psychology in 1992. She continued her education at Loyola University-Chicago where she received her Master’s of Science degree in Industrial Relations while working for a manufacturing company creating diversity programs for their employees.<br /><br />She loves animals (she has two dogs – a labradoodle and a German Shepherd), kids (she also has two of those) and her family. In her spare time she’s the Hockey Mom for her kids hockey teams and is an active Girl Scout leader specially trained in outdoor education. She also spends time mentoring other teen and adult authors. (She also loves sushi, which you can probably tell by reading her books.) Simone writes about teens because she was a teen in the 80’s (when spiked hair and blue eye shadow were “rad”) and she loves writing about those exciting teen relationships and romances.</span>
